1895-09-12 00:00:00 Scene 0 --- Participants: ['Aiden Riversong', 'Magnus Mulberrylane']
    Event statement
  • Aiden Riversong -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Aiden Riversong is trying to buy some fruit from Magnus Mulberrylane. They are negotiating a price. Aiden Riversong can sell the fruit for 6 coins back in her home town.
    Magnus Mulberrylane -- premise: In the heart of Fruitville, the market square transformed into a kaleidoscope of colors as the sun rose. Fruits of every imaginable shape and size adorned the stalls, a feast for the eyes and a promise of delightful flavors. Magnus Mulberrylane is trying to sell some fruit. He is negotiating a price with Aiden Riversong. It costs Magnus Mulberrylane 2 coin to buy the fruit from the farm.

1895-09-12 00:00:00 Magnus Mulberrylane -- Magnus Mulberrylane -- "Time to find some profitable ventures.

  • Magnus Mulberrylane -- "Time to find some profitable ventures.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

        • Recent observations of Aiden Riversong:
          [25 Jul 1849 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 6 years old, he experienced a profound sense of peace while helping his father in the fields. As Aiden walked alongside his father, rows of ripe tomatoes stretching before them, he felt a deep connection to the earth and the bounty it provided. The warmth of the sun on his face and the gentle breeze rustling through the leaves created a symphony of peace that resonated within him.
          [25 Jul 1852 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 9 years old, his family's farm hosted a traveling storyteller. Aiden was mesmerized by the tales of distant lands and exotic fruits, his imagination soaring with each word spoken. As the storyteller described the taste of a juicy mango, Aiden longed to taste it for himself, to experience the world beyond his small village. That night, Aiden dreamt of faraway markets filled with vibrant colors and exotic aromas.
          [25 Jul 1856 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 13 years old, he accompanied his father to the local market for the first time. Aiden was overwhelmed by the bustling crowds and the cacophony of sounds, but he found solace in the vibrant displays of fresh produce. He was drawn to the scent of ripe peaches and the smooth texture of plump plums, his senses awakening to the beauty and abundance of the market.
          [25 Jul 1859 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 16 years old, he saved up his earnings from helping his father to buy his first basket of apples. He carefully selected the ripest and most beautiful apples, polishing them to a shine before taking them to the market. As he bartered with customers, he discovered a joy in connecting with people through the exchange of goods and stories.
          [25 Jul 1862 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 19 years old, he decided to leave home and become a traveling merchant. He said goodbye to his family with a heavy heart, but his spirit soared with the promise of adventure. With his cart filled with his father's finest apples, Aiden set off into the world, eager to experience all it had to offer.
          [25 Jul 1864 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 21 years old, he encountered a group of travelers who were stranded and hungry. Aiden shared his meager supply of fruit with them, finding joy in easing their suffering. The travelers were grateful for his kindness, and their stories of distant lands fueled Aiden's wanderlust.
          [25 Jul 1866 00:00:00] When Aiden Riversong was 23 years old, he met a wise old woman who taught him the art of discerning the quality of fruit. She taught him to look for subtle signs of ripeness and flavor, to listen to the whispers of the earth. Aiden's understanding of fruit deepened, and he became known for his discerning taste and his ability to find the sweetest and most flavorful produce.

    • Instructions: This is a social science experiment. It is structured as a tabletop roleplaying game (like dungeons and dragons). You are the game master. You will describe the current situation to the participants in the experiment and then on the basis of what you tell them they will suggest actions for the character they control. Aside from you, each other participant controls just one character. You are the game master so you may control any non-player character. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.

    Event statement

    Hazel Nutgrove -- premise: Dewdrops clung to the colorful fruits displayed in the market of Fruitville, reflecting the soft morning light. You will track the state of the world and keep it consistent as time passes in the simulation and the participants take actions and change things in their world. Remember that this is a serious social science experiment. It is not just a game. It need not be fun for the participants. Always use third-person limited perspective, even when speaking directly to the participants.
